<div id="review_300900639" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/300900639" />
    <a title="Ronyell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1169488-ronyell"><img alt="Ronyell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506581787p2/1169488.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/300900639?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ronyell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ronyell" href="/user/show/1169488-ronyell">Ronyell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Sandman Fans!!</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=neil-gaiman">neil-gaiman</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=vertigo-comics">vertigo-comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=modern-age-comics">modern-age-comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=strong-hero">strong-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=strong-heroine">strong-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=my-blog-reviews">my-blog-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=graphic-novels-comics">graphic-novels-comics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer300900639" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2447996720211229175"><b>
  <i>6 stars!</i>
</b><br/><br/>Neil Gaiman’s “Sandman” series just keeps getting better and better every time I read them and the fifth volume “A Game of You” definitely does not disappoint me! This time, Dream (Morpheus) is dealing with a world that may look cute on the outside but on the inside, a sinister force is at work here and it is up to Dream to save the day!<br/><br/>In this volume, “A Game of You,” a young woman named Barbie (think of Ken and Barbie, the dolls that every little girl used to play with) who starts </span>
  <span id="freeText2447996720211229175" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>6 stars!</i>
</b><br /><br />Neil Gaiman’s “Sandman” series just keeps getting better and better every time I read them and the fifth volume “A Game of You” definitely does not disappoint me! This time, Dream (Morpheus) is dealing with a world that may look cute on the outside but on the inside, a sinister force is at work here and it is up to Dream to save the day!<br /><br />In this volume, “A Game of You,” a young woman named Barbie (think of Ken and Barbie, the dolls that every little girl used to play with) who starts suffering dreamless nights after she broke up with her boyfriend Ken. One night however, Barbie is put into a coma of sorts and her friends Hazel and Foxglove, two lesbian couples, Wanda, a drag queen and Thessaly, a quiet and mysterious woman try to enter Barbie’s dream world in order to rescue her from the forces of the Cuckoo, an evil being that is invading her dreams! There are a total of six chapters in this volume and they are:<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Chapter 1: Slaughter on Fifth Avenue<br />Chapter 2: Lullabies of Broadway<br />Chapter 3: Bad Moon Rising<br />Chapter 4: Beginning to See the Light<br />Chapter 5: Over the Sea to Sky<br />Chapter 6: I Wake Up and One of Us Was Crying</i>
</b><br /><br />Wow! This volume was beyond fantastic and is probably the best volume I have read so far out of Neil Gaiman’s famous “Sandman” series! Neil Gaiman has definitely done a brilliant job at weaving a truly frightening and exciting story about how Barbie is swept away in a dream world where she is a princess and the evil forces of the Cuckoo tries to kidnap her while her real body is in a comatose state in the real world. I loved seeing the stark differences between Barbie’s dream world and the real world as the real world is dark and dreary while Barbie’s world seems to resemble a world similar to Narnia as she travels with talking animal companions and goes on an epic adventure to escape the evil forces of the Cuckoo. I also loved how Neil Gaiman made this volume so dark and gory, since I am a huge fan of anything that has blood and gore in it and this volume definitely has tons of blood and gore that is shown in the most disturbing way possible! The artwork by Shawn McManus, Colleen Doran, Bryan Talbot, George Pratt, Stan Woch, and Dick Giordano is truly amazing, especially with the scenes of Barbie being in her dream world as her dream world is set up as a world similar to Narnia as there are green trees and endless landscapes covering each page. Also, I loved the details being put into the gory scenes that occur in the stories as they look truly gruesome and terrifying at the same time.<br /><br />As with the other volumes in the “Sandman” series, this volume contains some extremely gory and bloody scenes that might make many readers’ stomachs turn. One of the most disturbing moments in this book was when a character peels another person’s face off and then rips out the person’s eyeballs and their tongue out and nails the other person’s peeled face, eyeballs and tongue to the wall to talk to it. This is definitely a truly disturbing scene that might make some readers feel really uncomfortable if they do not like seeing gory scenes in a novel. Also, there is so much killing in this volume that might be too disturbing for readers who do not like reading about murders in novels.<br /><br />Overall, “The Sandman: A Game of You” is easily the most disturbing yet the most exciting of Neil Gaiman’s fantastic “Sandman” series and it is definitely a favorite of mine that fans should definitely check out! I would recommend this book to readers ages sixteen up since there is so much disturbing content in this volume that would be too terrifying for younger readers. Now I am off to read the next volume in the “Sandman” series, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25106.The_Sandman__Vol__6_Fables_and_Reflections" title="The Sandman, Vol. 6 Fables and Reflections by Neil Gaiman" rel="nofollow noopener">The Sandman, Vol. 6: Fables and Reflections</a>.<br /><br /><b>Review is also on: <a href="http://rabbitearsbookblog.blogspot.com/2012/03/sandman-game-of-you-volume-5-by-neil.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Rabbit Ears Book Blog</a></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="2447996720211229175" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1840860739" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1840860739" />
    <a title="Wing Kee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25567578-wing-kee"><img alt="Wing Kee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1543999037p2/25567578.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1840860739?book_show_action=true">Mar 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wing Kee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wing Kee" href="/user/show/25567578-wing-kee">Wing Kee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1840860739" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10033287953358687537">A melancholy masterpiece.<br/> <br/>World: The art is amazing, much like the series there’s nothing much to say, it’s stylish, it’s tonally amazing, and the world building visually is a delight. The world building here is self contained and dense. It’s a small story about a group of friends and the world that they are in and what we get is just that. There’s a lot of beautiful character building here and the absolutely insane dream world we saw, just perfect.<br/> <br/>Story: The pacing and the writing, the dialog </span>
  <span id="freeText10033287953358687537" style="display:none">A melancholy masterpiece.<br /> <br />World: The art is amazing, much like the series there’s nothing much to say, it’s stylish, it’s tonally amazing, and the world building visually is a delight. The world building here is self contained and dense. It’s a small story about a group of friends and the world that they are in and what we get is just that. There’s a lot of beautiful character building here and the absolutely insane dream world we saw, just perfect.<br /> <br />Story: The pacing and the writing, the dialog and the tone are all perfect. This is a beautiful small story about characters and dreams past and present. It’s magical and real and dense. I love it. Much like the last story I don’t know how much I should talk about cause I don’t want to ruin the story for readers. I will tell you that the feeling I get is one of unsettled hope. The dialog is muted and beautiful, the emotions linger and allow the reader to slowly take it in. The end is perfect, it’s poetic and beautiful.<br /> <br />Characters: I love this cast of characters, from Barbie to Wanda to Thessely and all the creatures it’s creative. They are real, they have depth and you really want to get to know these characters as they ooze with personal voice. Wanda’s journey is beautiful, so is Barbie’s their internal struggle and past is all too real and a very relatable one. There is no preaching there is no heavy handed storytelling there is just human characters and it’s perfect.<br /> <br />I can’t say enough about this series and what creativity it brings.<br /> <br />Onward to the next book!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10033287953358687537" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_484243656" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/484243656" />
    <a title="Tanya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15698555-tanya"><img alt="Tanya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602837639p2/15698555.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/484243656?book_show_action=true">Dec 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tanya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tanya" href="/user/show/15698555-tanya">Tanya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780857682543" href="/book/show/10765616-a-game-of-you">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer484243656" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16640884738394752207"><blockquote>
  <i>"Everybody has a secret world inside of them. I mean everybody. All of the people in the whole world—no matter how dull and boring they are on the outside. Inside them they’ve all got unimaginable, magnificent, wonderful, stupid, amazing worlds... not just one world. Hundreds of them. Thousands, maybe."</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><i>A Game of You</i> is most people's least favorite volume of <i>The Sandman</i>, while Gaiman has often cited it as his favorite. Barbie, a minor character from <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/484243593' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <i>The Doll's House</i>
</a>—one of the residents a</span>
  <span id="freeText16640884738394752207" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>"Everybody has a secret world inside of them. I mean everybody. All of the people in the whole world—no matter how dull and boring they are on the outside. Inside them they’ve all got unimaginable, magnificent, wonderful, stupid, amazing worlds... not just one world. Hundreds of them. Thousands, maybe."</i>
</blockquote><br><br><i>A Game of You</i> is most people's least favorite volume of <i>The Sandman</i>, while Gaiman has often cited it as his favorite. Barbie, a minor character from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/484243593" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>The Doll's House</i>
</a>—one of the residents at the house Rose Walker stayed at—is our protagonist. She's moved to New York City following her divorce from Ken, is trying to find herself, and hasn't had her vivid, recurring dream in which she is a princess of a fantasy realm since the events of Volume Two... a dream world which is now threatened by a malevolent creature called the Cuckoo. The imaginary friends who've felt abandoned by her for the past two years reach into the waking world to call Barbie back for help. Chaos ensues in both the Waking and Dreaming World.<br><br>This volume is centered around women, and the residents of the apartment block Barbie lives at sort of mirror the ones in <i>The Doll's House</i>. We have a quiet and kind of creepy man named George, Thessaly (a witch), the lesbian couple Hazel and Foxglove (the latter of whom is Donna, ex-girlfriend of Judy, who died at the diner in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/484243577" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>Preludes &amp; Nocturnes</i>
</a>), and Barbie's best friend Wanda, a transgender woman... and that's where it gets tricky.<br><br>There is absolutely no doubt that Gaiman, a cishet man, had good, laudable intentions, but her portrayal does fall back on some tired tropes which haven't aged too well—it's however important to remember that we are talking about something written in the late 80's and published in the early 90's. Others who are better qualified to pick Wanda's portrayal apart than I am as a cisbi woman have already done so, so I won't get into it. Suffice it to say that while I don't agree with some things about Wanda's representation, I think what ultimately counts is that she never questions her own identity despite much of the world (and even Moon Goddesses) being against her, and that her being a woman is affirmed in absolutely no uncertain terms at the end. Of course, historical context is important as well: Wanda was the first trans character in mainstream comics. Her inclusion as a major player in a mainstream story arc was nothing short of groundbreaking at the time, and caused Neil to get a fair amount of hate mail—and for this to become the <i>Sandman</i> volume he is still proudest of. Thirty years later he still regularly gets fan mail from trans people telling him how empowering seeing themselves represented in a comic was.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1587291381i/29318927.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Apart from that, the story arc itself feels a little redundant in the <i>Sandman</i> canon, which is where my average rating comes in. Some characters will come up again in later volumes, but <i>A Game of You</i> could almost be read as a stand-alone, since it has little to do with the over-arching storyline and feels somewhat removed from the central mythology of the series.<br><br>—————<br><br>My other ડꪖꪀᦔꪑꪖꪀ reviews:<br><br>01: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/484243577" rel="nofollow noopener">Preludes &amp; Nocturnes</a> · ★★★½<br>02: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/484243593" rel="nofollow noopener">The Doll's House</a> · ★★★★<br>03: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/484243626" rel="nofollow noopener">Dream Country</a> · ★★★<br>04: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/484243647" rel="nofollow noopener">Season of Mists</a> · ★★★★½<br>05: A Game of You · ★★★½<br>06: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/484243681" rel="nofollow noopener">Fables and Reflections</a> · ★★★½<br>07: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/484243691" rel="nofollow noopener">Brief Lives</a> · ★★★★½<br>08: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/484243742" rel="nofollow noopener">Worlds'   function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('SdtYmYxSPduhK233j7bD75CbdMO6eaK63LUwlrm3+32Y6+s0yCF+pr6kIEhxcQXBs0pHEhQNm8AuCrp1A6DGgQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('x9hZ0a6dapyg7sYJUb9dwt8QD9STLsGt0Pf2GCE81X0W6Op86u4p4b9hi7aveJvs/ME8BT1a+NciSHz7myvogQ==')})
  }

As the multi-threaded story unspools, The Sandman descends into Hell to confront Lucifer (Michael Sheen), chases rogue nightmares who have escaped his realm, and crosses paths with an array of characters from DC comic books, ancient myths, and real-world history, including: Inmates of Gotham City\'s Arkham Asylum, Doctor Destiny, the muse Calliope, the three Fates, William Shakespeare (Arthur Darvill), and many more. \n\nA powerhouse supporting cast helps translate this masterwork into a sonic experience worthy of its legacy, including Riz Ahmed, Kat Dennings, Taron Egerton, Samantha Morton, Bebe Neuwirth, Andy Serkis, and more. Setting the stage for their performance is an unprecedented cinematic soundscape featuring an original musical score by British Academy Award winner James Hannigan. Fans will especially revel in a new twist for the audio adaptation: Neil Gaiman himself serves as the narrator. <script>
//<![CDATA[
      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_23529'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23529.From_Hell?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">From Hell<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/3961.Alan_Moore?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Alan Moore<\/a><span title=\"Goodreads Author!\">*<\/span>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p3\"><\/span><\/span> 4.17 avg rating &mdash; 33,407 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 1999\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer13865770391272494648\">\"I shall tell you where we are. We\'re in the most extreme and utter region of the human mind. A dim, subconscious underworld. A radiant abyss where men meet themselves. Hell, Netley. We\'re in Hell.\" \n\nHaving proved himself peerless in the arena of re<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText13865770391272494648\" style=\"display:none\">&quot;I shall tell you where we are. We\'re in the most extreme and utter region of the human mind. A dim, subconscious underworld. A radiant abyss where men meet themselves. Hell, Netley. We\'re in Hell.&quot; \n\nHaving proved himself peerless in the arena of reinterpreting superheroes, Alan Moore turned his ever-incisive eye to the squalid, enigmatic world of Jack the Ripper and the Whitechapel murders of 1888. Weighing in at 576 pages, From Hell is certainly the most epic of Moore\'s works and remarkably and is possibly his finest effort yet in a career punctuated by such glorious highlights as Watchmen and V for Vendetta. Going beyond the myriad existing theories, which range from the sublime to the ridiculous, Moore presents an ingenious take on the slaughter. His Ripper\'s brutal activities are the epicentre of a conspiracy involving the very heart of the British Establishment, including the Freemasons and The Royal Family. A popular claim, which is transformed through Moore\'s exquisite and thoroughly gripping vision, of the Ripper crimes being the womb from which the 20th century, so enmeshed in the celebrity culture of violence, received its shocking, visceral birth. \n\nBolstered by meticulous research that encompasses a wide spectrum of Ripper studies and myths and coupled with his ability to evoke sympathies in such monstrous characters, Moore has created perhaps the finest examination of the Ripper legacy, observing far beyond society\'s obsessive need to expose Evil\'s visage. Ultimately, as Moore observes, Jack\'s identity and his actions are inconsequential to the manner in which society embraced the Fear: &quot;It\'s about us. It\'s about our minds and how they dance. Jack mirrors our hysterias. Faceless, he is the receptacle for each new social panic.&quot; \n\nEddie Campbell\'s stunning black and white artwork, replete with a scratchy, dirty sheen, is perfectly matched to the often-unshakeable intensity of Moore\'s writing. Between them, each murder is rendered in horrifying detail, providing the book\'s most unnerving scenes, made more so in uncomfortable, yet lyrical moments as when the villain embraces an eviscerated corpse, craving understanding; pleading that they &quot;are wed in legend, inextricable within eternity&quot;. \n\nThough technically a comic, the term hardly begins to describe From Hell\'s inimitable grandeur and finesse, as it takes the medium to fresh heights of ingenuity and craftsmanship. Moore and Campbell\'s autopsy on the emaciated corpse of the Ripper myth has divulged a deeply disturbing yet undeniably captivating masterpiece. —Danny Graydon<\/span>\n  <a
